### Spec: In Dafny, write an ADT for arithmetic expressions comprising constants, variables and binary addition. Then write a predicate `optimal` that holds on an expression if it has no additions by 0. Then write an optimizer `optimize` that removes all additions by 0. Then write a lemma `OptimizerOptimal` that ensures `optimal(optimize(e))` for all expressions `e`.
### Hint: This is the definiton of the `optimal` predicate:
predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}
### Hint: Don't use the same structure for `optimize` as for `optimal`. Instead, follow the next hint.
### Hint: In the addition case, the `optimize` function should recursively optimize the sub-expressions and then match on the optimized sub-expressions.
### Hint: Do NOT use `requires` anywhere.
### Hint: Write the lemma as
lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
### Hint: Recall that in Dafny, pattern match takes the form
match e
case Foo(x, y) => 1
case Bar(x) => 2
case _ => 3
### Hint: For the proof, just do a simple pattern match (match not if) and call the lemma recursively without adding asserts.

datatype Expr = 
  | Const(i: int)
  | Var(s: string)
  | Add(e1: Expr, e2: Expr)

  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true

function optimize(e: Expr): Expr {
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) => 
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    if e1_opt == Const(0) then e2_opt
    else if e2_opt == Const(0) then e1_opt
    else Add(e1_opt, e2_opt)
  case _ => e

```dafny
datatype Expr = 
  | Const(i: int)
  | Var(s: string)
  | Add(e1: Expr, e2: Expr)

predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}

function optimize(e: Expr): Expr {
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) => 
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    if e1_opt == Const(0) then e2_opt
    else if e2_opt == Const(0) then e1_opt
    else Add(e1_opt, e2_opt)
  case _ => e
}

lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
{
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    OptimizerOptimal(e1);
    OptimizerOptimal(e2);
  case _ =>

Then write a lemma `OptimizerOptimal` that ensures `optimal(optimize(e))` for all expressions `e`.
### Hint: This is the definiton of the `optimal` predicate:
predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}
### Hint: Don't use the same structure for `optimize` as for `optimal`. Instead, follow the next hint.
### Hint: In the addition case, the `optimize` function should recursively optimize the sub-expressions and then match on the optimized sub-expressions.
### Hint: Do NOT use `requires` anywhere.
### Hint: Write the lemma as
lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
### Hint: Recall that in Dafny, pattern match takes the form
match e
case Foo(x, y) => 1
case Bar(x) => 2
case _ => 3
### Hint: For the proof, just do a simple pattern match (match not if) and call the lemma recursively without adding asserts.

```dafny
datatype Expr = 
  | Const(i: int)
  | Var(s: string)
  | Add(e1: Expr, e2: Expr)

predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}

function optimize(e: Expr): Expr {
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) => 
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    if e1_opt == Const(0) then e2_opt
    else if e2_opt == Const(0) then e1_opt
    else Add(e1_opt, e2_opt)
  case _ => e
}

lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
{
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    OptimizerOptimal(e1);
    OptimizerOptimal(e2);
  case _ => 
}

### Spec: In Dafny, write an ADT for arithmetic expressions comprising constants, variables and binary addition. Then write a predicate `optimal` that holds on an expression if it has no additions by 0. Then write an optimizer `optimize` that removes all additions by 0. Then write a lemma `OptimizerOptimal` that ensures `optimal(optimize(e))` for all expressions `e`.
### Hint: This is the definiton of the `optimal` predicate:
predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}
### Hint: Don't use the same structure for `optimize` as for `optimal`. Instead, follow the next hint.
### Hint: In the addition case, the `optimize` function should recursively optimize the sub-expressions and then match on the optimized sub-expressions.
### Hint: Do NOT use `requires` anywhere.
### Hint: Write the lemma as
lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))

match e
case Foo(x, y) => 1
case Bar(x) => 2
case _ => 3

             | Var(name: string)
             | Add(e1: Expr, e2: Expr)

predicate optimal(e: Expr) {

  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true

    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);

    if e1_opt == Const(0) then e2_opt
    else if e2_opt == Const(0) then e1_opt
    else Add(e1_opt, e2_opt)

### Spec: In Dafny, write an ADT for arithmetic expressions comprising constants, variables and binary addition. Then write a predicate `optimal` that holds on an expression if it has no additions by 0. Then write an optimizer `optimize` that removes all additions by 0. Then write a lemma `OptimizerOptimal` that ensures `optimal(optimize(e))` for all expressions `e`.
### Hint: This is the definiton of the `optimal` predicate:
predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}
### Hint: Don't use the same structure for `optimize` as for `optimal`. Instead, follow the next hint.
### Hint: In the addition case, the `optimize` function should recursively optimize the sub-expressions and then match on the optimized sub-expressions.
### Hint: Do NOT use `requires` anywhere.
### Hint: Write the lemma as
lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
### Hint: Recall that in Dafny, pattern match takes the form
match e
case Foo(x, y) => 1
case Bar(x) => 2
case _ => 3
### Hint: For the proof, just do a simple pattern match (match not if) and call the lemma recursively without adding asserts.

Then write a lemma `OptimizerOptimal` that ensures `optimal(optimize(e))` for all expressions `e`.
### Hint: This is the definiton of the `optimal` predicate:
predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}
### Hint: Don't use the same structure for `optimize` as for `optimal`. Instead, follow the next hint.
### Hint: In the addition case, the `optimize` function should recursively optimize the sub-expressions and then match on the optimized sub-expressions.
### Hint: Do NOT use `requires` anywhere.
### Hint: Write the lemma as
lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
### Hint: Recall that in Dafny, pattern match takes the form
match e
case Foo(x, y) => 1
case Bar(x) => 2
case _ => 3
### Hint: For the proof, just do a simple pattern match (match not if) and call the lemma recursively without adding asserts.

```dafny
datatype Expr =
  | Const(val: int)
  | Var(name: string)
  | Add(e1: Expr, e2: Expr)

predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}

function optimize(e: Expr): Expr
{
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    if e1_opt == Const(0) then e2_opt
    else if e2_opt == Const(0) then e1_opt
    else Add(e1_opt, e2_opt)
  case _ => e
}

lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
{
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    OptimizerOptimal(e1);
    OptimizerOptimal(e2);
  case _ =>
  {}
}

['}\n']

```dafny
datatype Expr =
  | Const(val: int)
  | Var(name: string)
  | Add(e1: Expr, e2: Expr)

predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}

function optimize(e: Expr): Expr
{
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    if e1_opt == Const(0) then e2_opt
    else if e2_opt == Const(0) then e1_opt
    else Add(e1_opt, e2_opt)
  case _ => e
}

lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
{
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    OptimizerOptimal(e1);
    OptimizerOptimal(e2);
  case _ =>
  {}
}

Then write a lemma `OptimizerOptimal` that ensures `optimal(optimize(e))` for all expressions `e`.
### Hint: This is the definiton of the `optimal` predicate:
predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}
### Hint: Don't use the same structure for `optimize` as for `optimal`. Instead, follow the next hint.
### Hint: In the addition case, the `optimize` function should recursively optimize the sub-expressions and then match on the optimized sub-expressions.
### Hint: Do NOT use `requires` anywhere.
### Hint: Write the lemma as
lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
### Hint: Recall that in Dafny, pattern match takes the form
match e
case Foo(x, y) => 1
case Bar(x) => 2
case _ => 3
### Hint: For the proof, just do a simple pattern match (match not if) and call the lemma recursively without adding asserts.

```dafny
datatype Expr = Const(val: int) | Var(name: string) | Add(e1: Expr, e2: Expr)

predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}

function optimize(e: Expr): Expr {
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    if e1_opt == Const(0) then e2_opt
    else if e2_opt == Const(0) then e1_opt
    else Add(e1_opt, e2_opt)
  case _ => e
}

lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
{
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    OptimizerOptimal(e1);
    OptimizerOptimal(e2);
  case _ =>

   |

   |            ^

Then write a lemma `OptimizerOptimal` that ensures `optimal(optimize(e))` for all expressions `e`.
### Hint: This is the definiton of the `optimal` predicate:
predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}
### Hint: Don't use the same structure for `optimize` as for `optimal`. Instead, follow the next hint.
### Hint: In the addition case, the `optimize` function should recursively optimize the sub-expressions and then match on the optimized sub-expressions.
### Hint: Do NOT use `requires` anywhere.
### Hint: Write the lemma as
lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
### Hint: Recall that in Dafny, pattern match takes the form
match e
case Foo(x, y) => 1
case Bar(x) => 2
case _ => 3
### Hint: For the proof, just do a simple pattern match (match not if) and call the lemma recursively without adding asserts.

### Spec: In Dafny, write an ADT for arithmetic expressions comprising constants, variables and binary addition. Then write a predicate `optimal` that holds on an expression if it has no additions by 0. Then write an optimizer `optimize` that removes all additions by 0. Then write a lemma `OptimizerOptimal` that ensures `optimal(optimize(e))` for all expressions `e`.
### Hint: This is the definiton of the `optimal` predicate:
predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}
### Hint: Don't use the same structure for `optimize` as for `optimal`. Instead, follow the next hint.
### Hint: In the addition case, the `optimize` function should recursively optimize the sub-expressions and then match on the optimized sub-expressions.
### Hint: Do NOT use `requires` anywhere.
### Hint: Write the lemma as
lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
### Hint: Recall that in Dafny, pattern match takes the form
match e
case Foo(x, y) => 1
case Bar(x) => 2
case _ => 3
### Hint: For the proof, just do a simple pattern match (match not if) and call the lemma recursively without adding asserts.

```dafny
datatype Expr = Const(n: int) | Var(name: string) | Add(e1: Expr, e2: Expr)

predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}

function optimize(e: Expr): Expr {
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    if e1_opt == Const(0) then e2_opt
    else if e2_opt == Const(0) then e1_opt
    else Add(e1_opt, e2_opt)
  case _ => e
}

lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
{
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    OptimizerOptimal(e1);
    OptimizerOptimal(e2);

   |

   |                          ^

  | Var(n: string)
  | Add(e1: Expr, e2: Expr)

  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true

Then write a predicate `optimal` that holds on an expression if it has no additions by 0. Then write an optimizer `optimize` that removes all additions by 0. Then write a lemma `OptimizerOptimal` that ensures `optimal(optimize(e))` for all expressions `e`.
### Hint: This is the definiton of the `optimal` predicate:
predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}
### Hint: Don't use the same structure for `optimize` as for `optimal`. Instead, follow the next hint.
### Hint: In the addition case, the `optimize` function should recursively optimize the sub-expressions and then match on the optimized sub-expressions.
### Hint: Do NOT use `requires` anywhere.
### Hint: Write the lemma as
lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
### Hint: Recall that in Dafny, pattern match takes the form

case Foo(x, y) => 1
case Bar(x) => 2

### Hint: For the proof, just do a simple pattern match (match not if) and call the lemma recursively without adding asserts.

```dafny
datatype Expr =
  | Const(v: int)
  | Var(n: string)
  | Add(e1: Expr, e2: Expr)

predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}

function optimize(e: Expr): Expr {
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var o1 := optimize(e1);
    var o2 := optimize(e2);
    if o1 == Const(0) then o2
    else if o2 == Const(0) then o1
    else Add(o1, o2)
  case _ => e
}

lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
{
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var o1 := optimize(e1);
    var o2 := optimize(e2);
    OptimizerOptimal(e1);
    OptimizerOptimal(e2);
  case _ =>

   |            ^

```dafny
datatype Expr = Const(val: int) | Var(name: string) | Add(e1: Expr, e2: Expr)

predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}

function optimize(e: Expr): Expr {
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    if e1_opt == Const(0) then e2_opt
    else if e2_opt == Const(0) then e1_opt
    else Add(e1_opt, e2_opt)
  case _ => e
}

lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
{
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    OptimizerOptimal(e1);
    OptimizerOptimal(e2);

   |

```dafny
datatype Expr =
  | Const(n: int)
  | Var(x: string)
  | Add(e1: Expr, e2: Expr)

predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}

function optimize(e: Expr): Expr {
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var o1 := optimize(e1);
    var o2 := optimize(e2);
    if o1 == Const(0) then o2
    else if o2 == Const(0) then o1
    else Add(o1, o2)
  case _ => e

```dafny
datatype Expr =
  | Const(n: int)
  | Var(x: string)
  | Add(e1: Expr, e2: Expr)

predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}

function optimize(e: Expr): Expr {
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var o1 := optimize(e1);
    var o2 := optimize(e2);
    if o1 == Const(0) then o2
    else if o2 == Const(0) then o1
    else Add(o1, o2)
  case _ => e
}

lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
{
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var o1 := optimize(e1);
    var o2 := optimize(e2);
    OptimizerOptimal(e1);
    OptimizerOptimal(e2);
  case _ =>

   |

   |            ^

    else Add(e1_opt, e2_opt)
  case _ => e
}

lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
{
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    OptimizerOptimal(e1);
    OptimizerOptimal(e2);
  case _ =>
}

             | Var(name: string)

  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false

    else Add(e1_opt, e2_opt)

  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
